فعلى هذا التقدير الحق مقصد يه هو كه اگر قرآن نام هو اس مؤلف مخصوص كا اور حق بهى يهى هيفر اشكال يه تها كه اس تقرير حق كے مطابق قرآن شخصى نهيں رهے گا بلكه تعدد كو قبول كرے گا تو اس كا جواب مصنف نے يه ديا كه اس صورت ميں قرآن پاك كے شخصى ہونے كى دو تاويليں ہوں گى اول يه كه قرآن كے شخصى ہونے كا مطلب يه ہوگا كه وه خود تو شخصى نهيں ہے البتہ شخصى كے مشابہ ہے مشابہت يه ہے كه جس طرح شخصى حد كو قبول نهيں كرتا اس كى معرفت اشاره وغيرہ كے ساتھ هوتى ہے اسی طرح قرآن مجيد بهى قابل حد نهيں بلكه اس كى حقيقت كى معرفت اس طرح ہوگى كه اس كو اول تا آخر پڑها جائے اور پهر كها جائے بالاشاره كه هو هذه الكلمات بهذا الترتيب اور دوسرى تاويل يه كى جائے گى كه وه مؤلف مخصوص جوں ذاتہ متعدد نه هو بلكه اس كا تعدد محل كے تعدد كى وجه سے هوا اگر چه يه شخصى حقيقى نهيں ہے ليكن ہم نے اصطلاح بنالى ہے كه ہم اس شخصى كو حقيقى كهتے ہيں اور اس پر يه حكم لگاتے ہيں كه وه قابل حد نهيں ہے كيونكه اس كى معرفت يا اشاره سے حاصل هوتى ہے يا قراء من اوله الی آخره سے حاصل هوتى ہے لهذا يه شخصى ہے۔ ولا يخفى ان الكلام يه ما قبل كا تقه ہے مقصد يه ہے كه يه جو كها گيا ہے كه شخصى كى حد نهيں هو سكتى اس سے مراد حد حقيقى ہے كه اس كى حقيقت و ماهيت كى تحدید نهيں هوسكتی بلكه قرائت اور اشاره ضروری ہے اگر معرفت حقيقت من التحديد مقصود نه هو بلكه صرف شخصى كا امتياز عن الاغيار مقصود هو تو يه ممكن ہے مثلا شخصى كى حد یوں كی جائے القرآن هو المجموع المنقول بين دفتي المصاحف تو اترا تو يه حد امتياز عن الغير كا فائده دے رہى ہے اسی طرح كشاف كى تعريف كی جائے هو الكتاب الذى صفه جار الله زمخشری فی تفسير القرآن اور نو كى تعريف كی جائے هو علم بحث فی عن احوال الكلم اعراب و بناء يه سب شخصى كى ايسى حدود هيں جو اسے ممتاز عن الغير كر رہی هيں ۔قوله فان الاعراض تنتهى الخ : غرض شارح توضيح متن ! مقصد يه ہے كه اعراض اپنے مشخصات كى وجه سے ايسے مرتبہ تعين تك پہنچ جاتے هيں كه ان ميں تعدد كا امكان باقى نهيں رہتا صرف امر واحد پر صادق آتے هيں ہاں ان كے اندر تعد محل كى وجه سے تعدد هو سكتا ہے مثلا امرى القیس كا قصيدہ ہے، قفا نبك من ذكرى حبيب و منزل اب يه قصيدہ اپنے مشخصات يعنى تاليف مخصوص جو مخصوص حروف كلمات ابيات كى وجه سے حاصل هوئى ہے اسی طرح وه صيت جو حركات سكنات سے حاصل هوئى ہے ان مشخصات كى وجه سے ايسى حد تك پہنچ گيا ہے كه اس كى ذات ميں كوئى تعدد نهيں هو سكتا اور صدق على الكثير ممكن نهيں ہے البتہ تعدد لافظ كى وجه سے اس ميں تعدد هو سكتا ہے اب اگر اس كے ساتھ تشخص لافظ بهى ملا ديا جائے مثلاً يه اعتبار كر ليا جائے كه وه قصيدہ جو لسان امرى القيس كے ساتھ مخصوص وقت ميں قائم تھا تو پهر يه شخصى حقيقى بن جائے گا اور اس ميں تعدد اصلا ممكن نهيں ہوگا مصنف نے يه اصطلاح بنالى ہے كه وه ايسے مؤلف مخصوص كو شخصى حقيقى بننے سے قبل اور محل كے ساتھ قائم ہونے سے قبل شخصى كهتا ہے لا مشاحۃ فی الاصطلاح - قوله وقد عرف ابن الحاجب ظاهر تعريفه الخ شارح تفتازانی مصنف كے اعتراض علی ابن الحاجب كا جواب دينے كى كوشش كر رہے هيں دو احتمال تھے كه ابن الحاجب كى تعريف يا مجموع شخصى كی ہوگی يا مفہوم كلى كی ہمصنف نے دونوں پر اشكال كيا تھا شارح كهتے هيں كه ظاهر عبارة ابن الحاجب سے معلوم هوتا ہے كه تعريف مجموع شخصى كی ہے. وجه يه ہے كه اس نے بسورۃ منہ كها ہے يہ من تبعيضيه ہے اور منہ كى ضمير راجع الى الكلام المنزل ہے معنى ہوگا مجر من المجموع اس سے معلوم ہوا كه تعريف مجموع شخصى كی ہے تو دور لازم نهيں آئے گا اگر مفہوم كلى كى تعريف بنائی جائے يه بهى ممكن ہے وہ اس طرح كه منہ كى ضمير جنس قرآن كى طرف راجع ہو عبارت یوں ہوگی۔ مجرو من جنس القرآن يعنى وه سورۃ فصيح و بليغ هو جس طرح قرآن مجيد فصيح و بليغ ہے تو پهر يه مفہوم كلى كى تعريف ہوگی شارح کهتے هيں كه دونوں صورتوں ميں ازوم دور نهيں ہوگا كيونكه معرفت قرآن تو موقوف ہے ماهيت سورۃ پر لكن ماهيت سورۃ ماهيت قرآن پر موقوف نهيں ہے كيونكه سورۃ كى تعريف ہے، جو بعض مترجم اولہ و آخرہ تو قیفا من كلام منزل اب اس كى معرفت قرآن پر موقوف ہے كيونكه يه عام ہے قران غير قرآن سب كو شامل ہے كيونكه توراة، انجيل كے سور كو بهى سور كها جاتا ہے معلوم ہوا كه سورۃ كے مفہوم ميں خصوصيت قرآن معتبر نهيں ہے يهى وجه ہے ابن الحاجب نے منہ كا لفظ ذكر كيا ہے تو ضمير راجع الی الكلام المنزل ہے اگر مفہوم سوره صرف قرآن كے ساتھ خاص هوتا تو منہ كے ذكر كرنے كى ضرورت نه ہوتى۔ جواب ! شارخ نے سورۃ كى جو تعريف كى ہے اور اس سے دور كو رفع كرنے كى كوشش كى ہے يه سعي لاحاصل ہے كيونكه يه تعريف عدول من الظاهر ہے كيونكه هر اصطلاح ميں اس كے اپنے مفہوم اصطلاحى مراد هوتے هيں اور شريعت كى اصطلاح ميں سورۃ كا مفہوم۔ وھی بعض من القرآن مترجم اولہ و آخرہ تو قیفا ہے يهى تعريف تفاسير معتبره كشاف وغيرہ ميں مذكور ہے لهذا اس سے عدول عدول عن الظاهر الی اٹھی، ومن الحقيقتہ الی المجاز ہوگا۔
Based on this assessment, the correct objective is that if the name 'Qur'an' applies to that specific composition, and indeed it is correct, then the objection is that according to this correct statement the Qur'an would not be individual but would admit multiplicity. The author answered that in that case there are two interpretations for the Qur'an being individual: first, that its being individual means it is not individual itself but resembles an individual, similar to how an individual does not accept definition and its knowledge is through pointing etc., similarly the Noble Qur'an is not definable but its reality is known by reading it from beginning to end and then saying by pointing 'it is these words in this order'. Second interpretation: that specific composition is not multiple in itself but its multiplicity is due to multiplicity of loci; although this is not real individuality, we have coined a convention that we call this individual real and apply the ruling that it is not definable because its knowledge is obtained either by pointing or by reading from beginning to end, hence it is individual. It is not hidden that the discourse is the culmination of what preceded. The objective is that what was said that 'the individual cannot be defined' means real definition, i.e., its reality and quiddity cannot be defined, rather reading and pointing are necessary. If knowledge of reality through definition is not intended but only distinguishing the individual from others is intended, then it is possible, e.g., defining the individual as 'the Qur'an is the totality transmitted between the covers of the mushafs' – this definition gives the benefit of distinguishing from others. Similarly, defining al-Kashshaf as 'the book authored by Jarallah al-Zamakhshari in tafsir of the Qur'an', and defining nahw as 'a science that investigates the states of words regarding i'rab and bina' – all these are definitions of the individual that distinguish it from others. His statement: 'for accidents end...' – the goal of the commentator of al-Tawdih: the objective is that accidents, due to their characteristics, reach such a degree of determination that multiplicity in them is no longer possible; they only apply to one thing. However, multiplicity can occur in them due to multiplicity of locus, e.g., the poem of Imru' al-Qays: 'Qifa nabki min dhikra habibin wa manzil'. This poem, due to its characteristics – i.e., the specific composition consisting of specific letters, words, and verses, and the sound composed of movements and pauses – has reached such a degree that there is no multiplicity in its essence and it cannot apply to many. However, multiplicity can occur due to multiplicity of utterance. If locative individuation is also added, e.g., considering that poem which existed with the tongue of Imru' al-Qays at a specific time, then it becomes real individual and multiplicity is absolutely impossible. The author made a convention that he calls such a specific composition before becoming real individual and before being established with a locus as 'individual' – no dispute in terminology. His statement: 'And Ibn al-Hajib defined...' The commentator al-Taftazani attempts to answer the author's objection against Ibn al-Hajib. There were two possibilities: Ibn al-Hajib's definition was either of the collective individual or the universal concept. The author objected to both. The commentator says that the apparent wording of Ibn al-Hajib indicates that the definition is of the collective individual. The reason is that he said 'bi-suratin minhu' – 'min' is partitive, and the pronoun in 'minhu' refers back to 'al-kalam al-munazzal'. The meaning would be 'a portion from the totality'. From this it is known that the definition is of the collective individual, and thus circularity does not occur. If it were made a definition of the universal concept, that is also possible, such that the pronoun in 'minhu' refers back to the genus of the Qur'an; the expression would be 'a surah from the genus of the Qur'an', meaning a surah that is eloquent and clear like the Qur'an. Then it would be a definition of the universal concept. The commentator says that in both cases circularity does not occur because knowledge of the Qur'an depends on the quiddity of surah, but the quiddity of surah does not depend on the quiddity of the Qur'an, because the definition of surah is 'a portion of revealed speech with a beginning and end'. Now its knowledge does not depend on the Qur'an because it is general and includes both Qur'an and non-Qur'an, since surahs of the Torah and Gospel are also called surah. It is known that specificity of the Qur'an is not considered in the concept of surah. This is why Ibn al-Hajib mentioned the word 'minhu', with the pronoun referring to 'al-kalam al-munazzal'. If the concept of surah were specific to the Qur'an, there would be no need to mention 'minhu'. Response: The commentator's definition of surah and his attempt to remove circularity is futile because this definition deviates from the apparent meaning, since in every discipline its own technical meaning is intended. In the terminology of Shari'ah, the concept of surah is 'a portion of the Qur'an with a beginning and end specifically revealed'. This definition is mentioned in reliable tafsirs like al-Kashshaf and others. Therefore, deviation from this is deviation from the apparent to the obscure, and from the real to the metaphorical.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the commentator (probably the author of this Urdu sharh) on the definition of the Qur'an and surah, responding to an objection regarding circularity. The discussion begins with the concept of 'individual' (shakhsi) and its applicability to the Qur'an. The author explains that the Qur'an, being a specific composition, can be considered individual in a conventional sense, either by resembling an individual in being indefinable or by being multiple only due to multiplicity of loci. He then addresses the definition by Ibn al-Hajib, who defined the Qur'an as 'what is between the covers of the mushafs' or via a surah from it. The commentator (al-Taftazani) defends Ibn al-Hajib by showing that his definition can be interpreted either as the collective individual or the universal concept, neither leading to circularity because the definition of surah does not depend on the Qur'an. However, the author of this sharh (the Urdu commentator) rejects this defense, arguing that the Shari'ah definition of surah is specifically 'a portion of the Qur'an', not general speech. Thus, the commentator's attempt fails.

Key Terms
شخصی (shakhsi): An individual entity that does not admit multiplicity in its essence, either real or conventional.
مجموع شخصی (majmu' shakhsi): A composite individuality that aggregates parts but remains one in itself.
مفہوم کلی (mafhum kulli): A universal concept that can apply to multiple individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why does al-Taftazani's defense of Ibn al-Hajib fail?
A) Because it incorrectly assumes surah is a general concept.
B) Because it uses a definition of surah that is not from the Qur'an or Sunnah.
C) Because it deviates from the Shari'ah definition of surah, which is specifically a portion of the Qur'an.
D) Because it relies on the partitive 'min' which is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school insists that technical terms in usul al-fiqh must be defined according to Shari'ah usage, not general language, to avoid flawed definitions and circular reasoning.

Haqiqah vs Majaz: Defending 'Nazm' for the Qur'an
Responding to objection that 'nazm' implies poetry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish haqiqah from majaz and apply that distinction to defend the use of 'nazm' for the Qur'an in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A term's literal meaning (haqiqah) governs its ruling; metaphorical use (majaz) does not affect the literal application.

In this passage, an objection is raised: if we avoid 'lafz' for the Qur'an due to disrespect, why use 'nazm' when it can mean poetry (shi'r), which is condemned? Taftazani responds by distinguishing haqiqah from majaz — the literal meaning of 'nazm' (stringing pearls) is noble, while the poetic sense is merely a metaphorical extension. Understanding this distinction is essential for usul al-fiqh, where the correct categorization of words determines legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection's basis
The objector argues that 'nazm' is disrespectful because one of its meanings is 'poetry', which is condemned in the Qur'an and hadith. Identify this reasoning in the passage.
The objection relies on the assumption that any possible meaning of a term, even a metaphorical one, affects its applied connotation.
2
Distinguish haqiqah from majaz
Taftazani states that the meaning 'poetry' is majaz (metaphorical), while the haqiqah (literal meaning) is 'stringing pearls'. In usul al-fiqh, haqiqah takes precedence over majaz unless a qarinah (contextual indicator) specifies otherwise. Note how this principle resolves the objection.
The literal meaning here is noble; thus, no disrespect follows.
3
Apply the usul rule
Apply the Hanafi rule: 'Al-haqiqah tufidu al-hukm al-asli; al-majaz la yu'taddu illa bi qarinah.' (The literal meaning yields the original ruling; the metaphorical is not considered unless there is an indicator.) Conclude that 'nazm' is used in its haqiqah, so it is permissible and respectful.
This prevents misapplication of terms based on secondary meanings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قيل كما ان اللفظ يطلق على الرمي الخ غرض جواب سوال ۔ سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ آپ نے الفاظ قرآن کو نظم کے ساتھ اسی لیے تعبیر کہا کہ لفظ کے اطلاق میں بے ادبی تھی تو شبہ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ نظم کے اطلاق میں بھی سوء ادب ہے کیونکہ نظم کا ایک معنی شعر بھی ہے اور قرآن پاک و احادیث میں اشعار و شعراء کی مذمت کی گئی ہے لہذا اس معنی اعتبار سے نظم کا اطلاق على الفاظ القرآن سوء ادب ہے ۔ جواب ! شارخ نے جواب دیا کہ نظم بمعنی شعر مجازی معنی ہے جب کہ نظم کا حقیقی معنی جمع اللؤلؤ فی السلکہے جو کہ بہت ہی عمدہ معنی ہے اور یہاں اسی لغوی و حقیقی معنی کے اعتبار سے اس کا اطلاق کیا گیا ہے جبکہ لفظ کے
If it is said: just as lafz is used for throwing... the purpose is to answer an implicit question. The question: You called the words of the Qur'an 'nazm' because using 'lafz' was disrespectful, but there is a doubt that using 'nazm' is also disrespectful because nazm has a meaning of poetry, and the Qur'an and hadith condemn poetry and poets. Therefore, applying nazm to the words of the Qur'an is disrespectful in that sense. The commentator answered that nazm meaning poetry is a metaphorical meaning, while the real meaning of nazm is 'strring pearls in a thread', which is a very noble meaning. Here it is applied in that literal and real sense, whereas lafz...
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage presents a final objection: if we avoid using 'lafz' for the Qur'an because it implies disrespect, the same might be said for 'nazm' since it can mean poetry, which is condemned. Taftazani responds that the poetic meaning is metaphorical; the literal meaning (stringing pearls) is honorable and suits the Qur'an. The passage is cut off, but the response is clear.

Key Terms
حقيقة (haqiqah): The literal, original meaning of a word as established in the language, used without a contextual indicator (qarinah) to the contrary.
مجاز (majaz): A metaphorical or transferred meaning that deviates from the literal sense and requires a contextual indicator (qarinah) to be valid.
نظم (nazm): Literally 'stringing pearls', used technically for the composition of the Qur'an. Its metaphorical meaning is 'poetry'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Taftazani's response in the passage, why is using 'nazm' for the Qur'an not disrespectful despite its meaning 'poetry'?
A) Because poetry is not actually condemned in the Qur'an
B) Because 'poetry' is a metaphorical meaning, while the literal meaning is 'stringing pearls'
C) Because 'nazm' is a technical term that never meant poetry
D) Because the objection only applies to 'lafz', not 'nazm'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle that haqiqah (literal meaning) governs application, and majaz (metaphorical) requires a qarinah, resolves the objection that 'nazm' implies poetry.

Overlap Across Divisions: Defending Multiple Classifications
Addresses an objection that categories across divisions overlap

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why categories from different Hanafi usul divisions can overlap and apply the principle that exclusivity is required only within a single division.

Core Idea
Categories across different divisions can overlap; exclusivity is only required within each division.

In Hanafi usul, words are classified using multiple divisions (e.g., 'aam/khass, mushtarak/mutlaq). A keen student might notice that a word can belong to categories from different divisions at once—for instance, a word that is both 'aam (general) and mushtarak (homonym). This overlap might seem to violate the principle that categories in a division must be mutually exclusive. This passage from a classical usul text addresses that objection and clarifies the underlying principle: each division considers a different aspect, so overlap across divisions is perfectly acceptable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Understand the critic's claim: It is a fundamental rule that in any division, the categories must be mutually exclusive (al-taba'ini). But here, categories from different divisions appear to overlap. For example, a word like 'ayn is both 'aam (including all individuals of its meaning) and mushtarak (having multiple meanings).
The objection is based on a misunderstanding of which level exclusivity applies.
2
Recognize the Hanafi Principle
Learn the key principle: Exclusivity is required within a single division, not across different divisions. Each division is based on a distinct perspective (jihah), so categories from different divisions can coexist in one word.
This principle is fundamental to Hanafi classification methodology.
3
Apply the Example from the Passage
Work through the example given: Nouns have one division into mu'rab (inflected) and mabni (indeclinable), and another into ma'rifah (definite) and nakirah (indefinite). A word like 'Zaid' is both mu'rab and ma'rifah—but this is not a contradiction because these belong to two different divisions.
Within each division (mu'rab/mabni or ma'rifah/nakirah), the categories are exclusive; across divisions they are not.
4
Understand the Second Answer
If one insists on exclusivity across all categories, then the exclusivity becomes relative (i'tibari) and must be qualified by perspective (e.g., 'aam from one aspect, mushtarak from another). This preserves the logical consistency while acknowledging overlap.
This second answer shows flexibility in the Hanafi approach.

العمدة في ذالك الاستقراء الا ان هذا وجه ضبطه مقصد عبارت یہ ہے کہ اگر چہ ہم نے ان تقسیمات اربعہ کی دلیل حضر اور وجہ ضبط بیان کر دی ہے لیکن یہ تقسیمات و اقسام استقرائی ہیں اور استقرائی میں مزید اقسام کا احتمال موجود رہتا ہے ( منظر ( فان قلت من حق الاقسام التباين غرض سوال و جواب۔ سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ ضابطہ مسلمہ ہے کر تقسیم ہے جو اقسام نکلتے ہیں ان میں تباین و تغایر ضروری ہوتا ہے جبکہ ان اقسام میں تباین و تفاسیر نہیں ہے ایک لفظ میں جمع ہو سکتی ہیں مثلا لفظ مین مشترک بھی ہے عام بھی وغیرہ قلت سے دو جواب دے رہے ہیں حاصل جواب یہ ہے کہ ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ ایک تقسیم کے اقسام کا آپس میں تباین ضروری ہے اگر تقسیمات متعددہ ہوں تو ان کا آپس میں تباین ضروری نہیں ہے یہاں مختلف حیثیات سے مختلف تقسیمات ہیں لہذا ان تمام تقسیمات کے اقسام میں تباین ضروری نہیں ہے البتہ ہر تقسیم کے اقسام کا آپس میں تغایر ضروری ہے اور یہ ہر تقسیم میں موجود ہے جیسا کہ اسم کی ایک تقسیم معرب منی کی طرف ہے دوسری تقسیم معرفہ نکرہ کی طرف اب معرب منی میں تو تغایر ہے اسی طرح معرفہ نکرہ میں بھی تعارض ہے ایک ہی اسم معرفہ اور نکرہ نہیں ہو سکتا لیکن معرب منی اور نکرہ معرفہ کا آپس میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے ایک ہی اسم معرب بھی ہو معرفہ بھی ہو ایسا ہو سکتا ہے جیسے زید على انه لم يجعل الجميع اقساما متقابلہ سے دوسرا جواب دے رہے ہیں جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر ان تمام اقسام میں تباین و تغایر کرنا مقصود ہو تو پھر وہ تباین ذاتی نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اعتباری ہوگا پھر حیثیت کی قید لگانی پڑے گی مثلا پہلی تقسیم لفظ مین ہے یہ عام ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ آنکھ کے تمام افراد کو شامل ہے اور مشترک ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ بھر اور سورج سونا وغیرہ تمام معانی کو شامل ہے ( والله اعلم بالصواب)
The basis of that is induction, but this is a way to regulate it. The meaning of the phrase is: Although we have explained the exclusive proof and method of regulation for these four divisions, these divisions and categories are inductive, and induction leaves room for additional categories. (Objection): If you say: It is an accepted principle that in a division, the categories must be mutually exclusive. But in these categories, there is no exclusivity; they can be combined in one word. For example, the word 'ayn is both mushtarak and 'aam, etc. Answer: He gives two answers. The summary of the answer is: The principle is that within a single division, the categories must be mutually exclusive. If there are multiple divisions, they need not be mutually exclusive. Here, due to different perspectives, there are different divisions. Therefore, there is no need for mutual exclusivity across all divisions. However, within each division, mutual exclusivity is necessary, and that exists in each division. For example, one division of nouns is mu'rab/mabni, another is ma'rifah/nakirah. In mu'rab/mabni there is mutual exclusivity, similarly in ma'rifah/nakirah. A noun cannot be both ma'rifah and nakirah simultaneously. But mu'rab and ma'rifah can coexist; a noun can be both mu'rab and ma'rifah, like Zaid. (Second answer): If, however, one intends mutual exclusivity among all these categories, then that exclusivity would not be essential but rather relative, and then one would need to add a restriction of perspective. For example, in the first division of the word 'word', it is 'aam from the perspective of including all individuals of its meaning, and it is mushtarak from the perspective of including (all meanings like sea, sun, gold, etc.) And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage defends the classification system against an objection: that the categories from different divisions overlap (e.g., a word can be both 'aam and mushtarak). The answer is that within each division, the categories are exclusive, but across divisions they can combine because each division looks at a different aspect. An example: nouns have one division into mu'rab (inflected) and mabni (indeclinable), and another into ma'rifah (definite) and nakirah (indefinite). A word like 'Zaid' is both mu'rab and ma'rifah; these categories are not contradictory because they come from different classifications. If one insists on exclusivity across all divisions, then one must qualify each category with its perspective (e.g., 'aam from one aspect, mushtarak from another). This is a standard Hanafi usul defense of multiple classifications.

Key Terms
عام ('aam): A general term that includes all individuals of its meaning without restriction.
مشترک (mushtarak): A homonym: a word with multiple distinct meanings.
معرب (mu'rab): An inflected word whose ending changes according to grammatical function.
مبني (mabni): An indeclinable word whose ending does not change.
معرفة (ma'rifah): A definite noun (e.g., proper noun, preceded by alif lam).
نكرة (nakirah): An indefinite noun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why can a noun be both mu'rab and ma'rifah?
A) Because mu'rab and ma'rifah are not mutually exclusive within their own division.
B) Because they belong to two different divisions (mu'rab/mabni and ma'rifah/nakirah).
C) Because mu'rab is a type of ma'rifah.
D) Because the passage allows all categories to overlap without restriction.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, categories from different classifications can coexist in the same word because exclusivity is required only within each individual division.

Fakhral-Islam's Four Divisions of Textual Interpretation
Explains Fakhral-Islam's precise wording for each of the four classifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four divisions of textual interpretation in Hanafi usul as defined by Fakhral-Islam and explain the precise meaning of the terms used in each division.

Core Idea
Fakhral-Islam's four divisions analyze textual interpretation from the perspectives of coinage, usage, clarity, and listener comprehension.

In this passage, Taftazani unpacks Fakhral-Islam's precise captions for the four fundamental divisions of textual interpretation in Hanafi usul. Understanding these divisions is essential for correctly classifying texts and deriving rulings. We will examine each division, clarify the key terms, and resolve a common confusion about the first division.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Four Division Headings
Identify Fakhral-Islam's wording for each of the four divisions as quoted in the passage. Look for the phrases beginning with 'التقسيم الأول', 'التقسيم الثاني', etc.
The headings are: division 1 about arrangement (sigha and lugha), division 2 about usage, division 3 about clarification, division 4 about knowing the ways of stopping.
2
Analyze the First Division: Sigha and Lugha
Understand the debate: Some say sigha and lugha are synonyms; the author refutes this. Sigha is the form (shape, vocalization), lugha is the root (material letters). Together they constitute wad' (coining). The division focuses on how the word indicates meaning through its coined form and matter.
He gives the example of 'daraba': root letters for hitting, form for past tense.
3
Understand the Second Division: Usage
This division concerns the ways (wujuh) the text is used: haqiqah (original meaning) vs. majaz (transferred), and sarih (explicit) vs. kinayah (implicit). It is about how the text operates in clarifying meaning.
The phrase 'fi wujuh isti'mal dhalika al-nazm wa jaryanihi fi bab al-bayan' captures this.
4
Grasp the Third Division: Levels of Clarity
This division deals with the ways of clarifying meaning and its levels, specifically the categories of zahir (apparent), nass (clear text), etc. It is about the degree of clarity in the expression.
Fakhral-Islam says 'fi wujuh al-bayan bi dhalika al-'azim' – by that great word.
5
Comprehend the Fourth Division: Listener's Knowledge
This division is about the methods by which a listener arrives at the intended meaning. It focuses on the ways knowledge is conveyed to the hearer.
Taftazani explains it as 'ma'rifat al-turuq al-mu'arrifah li al-sami''.

بیان میں ہے باعتبار نفس معنی کے نہ کہ باعتبار متکلم یا سامع کے (۲) مصنف کا نظریہ یہ ہے کہ صیغہ ولغت سے وضع مراد ہے کیونکہ صیفہ کی تعریف ہے وہ شکل و صورت جو لفظ کو حرکات و سکنات کے اعتبار سے اور بعض لفظ موجود ہے شکل وصورت کو شامل ہے۔ اس لیے لغتہ سے صرف بادہ مراد ہو گا تو اب عبارت اس طرح بن جائے گی التقسيم الاول فى وجوه النظم هيئة ومادة اور قیمت و مادہ دونوں مل کر کنایہ ہیں وضعا سے تو حاصل عبارت کنایہ ہوگا ۔ وعن الثالث بقوله الخ تیسری تقسیم کو فخر الاسلام نے ان الفاظ سے تعبیر کیا ہے فی وجوہ البیان بذالک العظیم ای فی طرق اظہار المعنی و مراتبہ یعنی تیسری تقسیم اظہار معنی اور اس کے مراتب کے طرق کے بیان میں ہے یعنی ظاہر نص، وغیرہ وجن الرابع یعنی چوتھی تقسیم کو ان الفاظ سے تعبیر کیا فی معرفة وجوه الوقوف على المراد و المعاني اي معرفة الطرق سے تفتازانی وضاحت کر رہے ہیں کہ چوتھی تقسیم سامع کی اطلاع کے طریقوں کی معرفت کے بارے میں
His statement: 'And this is what Fakhral-Islam said' - The commentator Taftazani's purpose is to explain the words with which Fakhral-Islam expressed the four divisions. So the first division Fakhral-Islam expressed with these words: 'The first division concerning aspects of the text: form and language.' That is, the first division concerns the aspects of arrangement; in terms of form and language. Now a question arises: what is meant by form and language? Some say form and language are synonymous; by 'form' is meant the shape and appearance of the word, and by 'language' its root/morphemes. And it is due to these two things that a word indicates meaning. So the intent would be that the first division is concerning the aspects of arrangement according to the meaning itself, not according to the speaker or hearer. (2) The author's view is that by form and language is meant 'wad' (coining). Because the definition of form is the shape that a word obtains from its vowels and consonants and from the order of letters. And the meaning of language is also 'the coined word', i.e., the word coined for meaning. For meaning, two things are coined: the root consisting of letters, and second, the form/shape of the word. For example, the coiner of 'daraba' coined its root letters for the meaning of hitting, and its form for the past tense. So the word includes both root and form. But here the word 'form' already includes the shape, so by 'language' only the root is meant. Now the expression would be: 'The first division concerning aspects of the arrangement: form and matter.' And form and matter together are a metonymy for wad'. So the resulting expression is: 'The first division concerning aspects of the arrangement from the perspective of wad'.' So the first division is in terms of wad', i.e., how the word indicates its meaning based on its root and form. And he expressed the second division with these words: 'Concerning aspects of the usage of that text and its operation in the chapter of clarification.' Taftazani explains: 'Wujuh' here means 'ways'. So the second division concerns the ways of using the text: if the word is used in its original meaning, it is haqiqah; if used in a transferred meaning, it is majaz. Or it concerns the ways of operation of the text in clarifying meaning: if it is direct, it is sarih; if indirect, it is kinayah. And concerning the third division, his statement: 'The third division: concerning aspects of clarification by that great word' i.e., concerning the ways of manifesting meaning and its levels. So the third division is about the ways of expressing meaning and its levels, i.e., zahir, nass, etc. And the fourth division he expressed with these words: 'Concerning knowledge of the ways of stopping at the intended meaning and meanings' i.e., knowledge of the ways. Taftazani explains that the fourth division is about the methods of informing the listener.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
Taftazani elaborates on Fakhral-Islam's precise captions for the four divisions in Hanafi usul. The first division is about the arrangement of the text from the perspective of wad' (how words were coined): the root and form of the word. The second division is about the usage of the text: whether it is haqiqah (literal) or majaz (figurative), and whether it is sarih (explicit) or kinayah (implicit). The third division is about the clarity of meaning: the levels of clarity (zahir, nass, etc.). The fourth division is about the methods by which a listener arrives at the intended meaning: the various ways of understanding. This passage shows the systematic nature of Hanafi usul in categorizing every aspect of textual interpretation.

Key Terms
صیغہ (sigha): The form/shape of a word, including its vocalization and letter order
لغت (lugha): The root/morphemes of a word; here it means the material letters of the word
وضع (wad'): The coining of a word for a meaning; the conventional assignment of a meaning to a word

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The usage of the text in haqiqah and majaz
B) The levels of clarity such as zahir and nass
C) The arrangement of the text from the perspective of wad' (coining)
D) The methods by which the listener understands

Key Takeaway
Fakhral-Islam's four divisions provide a comprehensive framework for analyzing texts in Hanafi usul, each focusing on a distinct aspect: coinage, usage, clarity, and listener comprehension.

The Hanafi Definition of Ta'wil: Conditions of Mushtarak and Ghalabat al-Ra'y
Defining ta'wil by stating what does and does not constitute it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ta'wil, identify its two essential conditions (mushtarak word and ghalabat al-ra'y), and distinguish it from other interpretive methods such as taghyir, qiyas, or applying a definitive proof.

Core Idea
Hanafi ta'wil is interpretation of a mushtarak word by dominant opinion, not certainty.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the term ta'wil has a precise meaning. It is not any interpretation, but a specific method for choosing among meanings of a word that has been coined for multiple possibilities. This passage clarifies what ta'wil is not and isolates its defining conditions: the word must be mushtarak (homonym) and the preference must be based on ghalabat al-ra'y (dominant opinion), not on certain proof. Understanding this distinction is key to appreciating how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from ambiguous texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The passage defines ta'wil by negation and then by positive conditions. First, note what the author says does NOT count as ta'wil.
Ta'wil is not a free-for-all interpretation.
2
List what is excluded from ta'wil
The passage states that if preference is given by a definitive proof (dalil qati'), by qiyas (analogy), or by khabar wahid (solitary report), it is not ta'wil. Also, if the word is not mushtarak (e.g., mujmal or difficult), its clarification is not ta'wil.
Exclusion helps sharpen the definition.
3
Extract the positive conditions
The passage concludes that for ta'wil to be included in 'ilm al-sighah, both conditions must be met: the word must be mushtarak and the preference must be based on ghalabat al-ra'y.
These are the two essential conditions.
4
Understand the type of evidence required
Ta'wil uses dominant opinion (zann ghalib), not certainty (qat'). This is a key epistemological point in Hanafi usul.
Contrast with taghyir which uses certainty.
5
Connect to 'ilm al-sighah
Ta'wil is a category within the knowledge of word forms because it involves the linguistic coinage (wad') of mushtarak words.
This situates ta'wil in the broader usul framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نے کسی ایک کو نفس صیغہ میں غور و فکر کر کے ترجیح نہ دی جائے بلکہ کسی دلیل قطعی کے ساتھ ترجیح دی جائے تو اس کو تاویل نہیں کہا جائے گا بلکہ تغیر کہا جائے گا اسی طرح اگر قیاس یا خبر واحد کے ساتھ ترجیح دی جائے اس کو بھی تأویل نہ کہا جائے گا اسی طرح اگر مشترک نہ ہو بلکہ یفی مشکل مجمل ہو اور ان کا خفاء دلیل قطعی یا غنی کے ساتھ زائل کیا جائے اس کو بھی تأویل نہیں کہا جاتا اور نہ ہی یہ اقسام نظم میں سے ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں وضع کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے تو تأویل کو اقسام العلم صیغہ دلغتہ میں شامل کرنے کیلئے من المشرک اور بغالب الرأی دونوں قیدوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔
If one does not give preference to any one [meaning] by pondering over the very wording, but gives preference by means of a definitive proof, then it will not be called ta'wil but rather 'taghayyur' (change). Similarly, if preference is given by qiyas or khabar wahid, that too will not be called ta'wil. Similarly, if the word is not mushtarak but rather is mujmal or difficult, and its ambiguity is removed by a definitive or sufficient proof, that too is not called ta'wil, nor will it be among the categories of order (nazm) because there is no element of linguistic coinage (wad') in it. Therefore, for ta'wil to be included in the categories of 'ilm al-sighah, both conditions of being mushtarak and being based on ghalabat al-ra'y are necessary.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the conditions that define ta'wil. The author begins by stating what is not ta'wil: if a preference between meanings is made using a definitive proof (dalil qati'), it is not ta'wil but rather a form of alteration (taghayyur). Similarly, if the preference is based on analogical reasoning (qiyas) or a solitary report (khabar wahid), it is not ta'wil. Furthermore, if the word is not mushtarak (having multiple meanings) but is ambiguous due to being mujmal or difficult and that ambiguity is lifted by a definitive proof, that is also not ta'wil. The reason is that ta'wil specifically involves a word that has been coined for multiple meanings (mushtarak) where the preferred meaning is chosen through dominant opinion (ghalabat al-ra'y), not through certain evidence. The passage concludes that to classify ta'wil among the divisions of 'ilm al-sighah (knowledge of word forms), both the condition of the word being mushtarak and the condition of relying on ghalabat al-ra'y are essential.

Key Terms
تأويل (ta'wil): Choosing one of the meanings of a mushtarak word based on ghalabat al-ra'y (dominant opinion), not on definitive proof.
مشترك (mushtarak): A word coined for multiple meanings equally.
غالب الرأي (ghalabat al-ra'y): A strong opinion (zann ghalib) that results from careful consideration, not certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does ta'wil require?
A) Any interpretation of any text
B) A mushtarak text and preference by dominant opinion (ghalabat al-ra'y)
C) A definitive proof (dalil qat'i) to prefer one meaning
D) Only an ambiguous (mujmal) text

Key Takeaway
Ta'wil in Hanafi usul is strictly defined: it applies only to mushtarak words when a meaning is preferred by dominant opinion, not by certainty or external proofs.

Definition of Sifah (Adjective) and Its Defense
Defining 'adjective' and defending it against objections about scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sifah (adjective), explain the objection regarding its comprehensiveness, and evaluate the two answers given by the author.

Core Idea
A sifah is a derived noun with its root meaning and a derived form; its definition must be precise to include all adjectives and exclude non-adjectives.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text defines the term 'sifah' (adjective) as a type of derived noun. It explains the condition 'with the weight of the derived form' and addresses an objection that the definition fails to cover adjectives with non-standard patterns like af'al and fa'lan. The author provides two nuanced answers, showing the flexibility of Hanafi usul in handling linguistic categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Read the definition of sifah given: it is a derived noun whose meaning is exactly the meaning of its root but with the weight of a derived form (e.g., fa'il, maf'ul).
2
Parse the definition elements
Identify the two conditions: (1) meaning is the root meaning exactly, and (2) it carries a derived morphological weight. Note that this excludes non-derived (solid) nouns and also nouns of time/place/instrument because their meaning is not conventionally expressed with a derived weight.
3
Understand the objection
The objector claims that the definition only applies to adjectives with patterns fa'il and maf'ul, and not to patterns like af'al (abyad), fa'lan (atshan), etc., rendering the definition non-comprehensive.
The objection is that the definition is not jami' (comprehensive).
4
Analyze the first answer
The first answer broadens 'derived weight' to mean any standard derived pattern (fa'il, maf'ul, af'al, fa'lan, etc.), so all genuine adjectives are included. This also includes nouns of place/time/instrument (like maqtal) as adjectives, which the author accepts, opposing the majority.
The author is willing to oppose the jumhur in investigative contexts.
5
Analyze the second answer
The second answer restricts 'derived weight' to the common genus of fa'il and maf'ul. It argues that all adjectives, including those with non-standard patterns, still belong to this genus (e.g., the pattern af'al is a subtype of fa'il), while nouns of place/time/instrument do not, so they are excluded.
This preserves the exclusion of place/time nouns.

مثال زید اور ہم جنس جامد کی
His statement: 'And also the apparent noun' — the purpose of the commentator is to explain the reason for the restriction 'apparent', to exclude pronouns and demonstrative nouns. So 'apparent' means 'that which is not a pronoun nor a demonstrative noun.' And 'the adjective' according to this division is a derived noun — the purpose is to clarify the definition of adjective: that the adjective is a derived noun whose meaning is exactly the meaning of its root, but with the weight of the derived form. For example, 'al-darib' is a word derived from 'darb', its meaning is 'the one who does darb', but the weight of the derived active participle is considered. Similarly, 'madrub' means 'darb with the weight of the passive participle'. And this is from their statement: i.e., some scholars defined the adjective as 'that which indicates an ambiguous essence and a specific meaning that subsists in that ambiguous essence.' The commentator says that this definition and the previous one have the same meaning. And by his statement 'with the weight of the derived form', he excluded nouns of time and instrument, because the meaning of 'maqtal' is not 'qatl with the weight of maf'al', and the meaning of 'miftah' is not 'fath with the weight of mif'al', because the one from whom the action issues is described by the active participle, and the one upon whom the action occurs is described by the passive participle, this is well-known and widespread. In contrast, naming a noun of place or instrument with the weights maf'al and mif'al is not well-known. One may object: This interpretation applies only to some adjectives. Here an objection is raised against the definition of adjective: that the definition is not comprehensive. Because the definition given is that its meaning is exactly the meaning of the root, but with the weight of the derived form. This definition applies only to adjectives that are with the weight of the active or passive participle. Other adjectives, despite being adjectives, are not covered by this definition because they are not expressed with a derived weight. For example, 'abyad' is not expressed as 'bayad with the weight of af'al', nor 'afdal' as 'afdaliyyah with the weight of af'al', nor 'atshan' as 'atsh with the weight of fa'lan', nor 'khayr' as 'khayriyyah with the weight of fa'l', nor 'mustakhraj' as 'istikhraj with the weight of mustaf'al', nor 'mudahraj' as 'dahrajah with the weight of mufa'lil'. All these are adjectives, but the definition does not apply to them. And if you deny that (i.e., claim that the definition does apply to these), then we say: what is the fault of nouns of place and instrument? They should also be included as adjectives, because expressing 'maqtal' as 'qatl with the weight of maf'al' is not more far-fetched than expressing 'abyad' as 'bayad with the weight of af'al' or 'mudahraj' as 'dahrajah with the weight of mufa'lil'. So both are equal. If those are excluded, these should also be excluded; if those are included, these should also be included. Answer: Two answers are given to this objection. (1) The first answer is that 'weight of the derived form' does not refer only to fa'il and maful, but rather the form and shape of the derived form. So the meaning is: the adjective is that whose meaning is exactly the meaning of its root with the form of a derived form, whether it is the form of fa'il, maful, mufa'lil, mustaf'al, etc. Thus all adjectives are included. But the question remains that then nouns of place, time, and instrument would also be included as adjectives, whereas the majority do not include them. The answer is that according to the author, they are included in adjectives because the definition applies to them. As for the majority, the author, in a place of investigation, opposes the majority, as he earlier opposed them in discussions of 'subject'. (2) The second answer is that 'weight of the derived form' means the weight of the genus of the derived form. If the meaning is 'derived', then all adjectives are of the genus of fa'il and maful, unlike the nouns of time, place, and instrument, whose weights are not from the genus of derived adjectives. His statement: 'Both of them, i.e., the proper noun and the common noun, are either derived or not' — purpose: clarifying the text 'know'. And the common noun is either derived: example of derived proper noun: Hatim; example of derived common noun: maqtal. And the example of 'darib' for a derived common noun is not valid because that is an example of an adjective, which is the counterpart and opposite of the common noun. Therefore, 'darib' cannot be an example of a derived common noun. Or both are not derived, but rather solid: example of solid proper noun: Zayd; example of solid common noun: ...
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the definition of 'adjective' (sifah) in usul al-fiqh. It begins by clarifying that 'apparent noun' (ism zahir) excludes pronouns and demonstratives. Then it defines an adjective as a derived noun whose meaning is identical to its root but carries a derived form (e.g., active participle fa'il, passive participle maf'ul). The author adds the condition 'with the weight of the derived form' to exclude nouns of time and instrument (e.g., maqtal, miftah) because their meaning is not conventionally expressed as root plus derived weight. An objection is raised that this definition fails to cover adjectives like 'abyad' (white) which have non-standard derived forms (e.g., af'al, fa'lan, etc.). The objector argues that if these are included, then nouns of time and instrument should also be included on equal footing. The author provides two responses: (1) 'derived weight' means any standard derived form, not just fa'il and maf'ul, so all adjectives are included; however, this would also include nouns of place/time/instrument, but the author accepts this consequence, opposing the majority. (2) Alternatively, 'derived weight' refers to the common patterns of fa'il and maf'ul; all adjectives follow these patterns, whereas nouns of place/time/instrument do not. Finally, the passage notes that proper nouns and common nouns can be either derived (e.g., Hatim, maqtal) or solid (e.g., Zayd). The example 'darib' is rejected as a derived common noun because it is an adjective, which is a separate category.

Key Terms
صفت (sifah): A derived noun indicating a meaning that subsists in an ambiguous essence, with a derived weight.
وزن مشتق (wazn mushtaq): The morphological pattern of a derived form (fa'il, maf'ul, etc.)
جامد (jamid): Non-derived (solid) noun, not derived from a root.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's second answer, why are nouns like 'maqtal' not considered adjectives?
A) Because they do not have a derived meaning.
B) Because their weight (maf'al) is not from the genus of fa'il and maf'ul.
C) Because they are not derived.
D) Because the majority excludes them.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of sifah is a derived noun with root meaning and derived form; it can be interpreted broadly to include all adjectives, and the author defends it against objections by specifying the scope of 'derived weight'.

Refining the Definition of Ṣifa (Adjective) in Hanafi Uṣūl
Critiquing and defending the definition of adjective (ṣifa)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ṣifa and apply the two responses to the critique regarding its inclusiveness to distinguish between adjectives and other derived nouns.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition of ṣifa is refined through debate: either all derived forms qualify, or only those from the genus of fāʿil and mafʿūl.

In Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh, the precise classification of words is foundational to legal interpretation. The definition of ṣifa (adjective) determines which words are considered descriptors that can affect rulings. This passage presents a critique that the standard definition is either too narrow or too broad, and then offers two responses that represent different Hanafi positions. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to analyze derived terms in legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the critique of the definition
Read the objection: the definition that ṣifa conveys the source meaning with a derived weight only applies to fāʿil and mafʿūl patterns, excluding other genuine adjectives like afʿal, fuʿlān, mustafʿil, mufaʿlil. Understand the examples given (abyad, ʿaṭshān, etc.).
The critique claims the definition is not comprehensive (ghayr jāmiʿ).
2
Analyze the counter-objection about ẓarf and āla
If one insists the definition does apply to those patterns, then nouns of place/time/instrument (e.g., maqtal) would also be included, since their derivation is similar. This exposes a potential over-inclusiveness problem.
The counter-objection uses the same logic to force an absurd consequence.
3
Examine the first response: broad interpretation
The first answer interprets 'wazn al-mushtaqq' broadly to mean any derived form or pattern, including mufaʿlil, mustafʿil, etc. This includes all adjectives but also includes ẓarf and āla nouns. The author accepts this, even against the majority.
This response sacrifices the exclusion of ẓarf/āla for inclusiveness of all adjectives.
4
Examine the second response: narrow by genus
The second answer restricts 'wazn al-mushtaqq' to weights that belong to the genus of fāʿil and mafʿūl. All genuine adjectives have patterns from this genus, while ẓarf and āla nouns do not. Thus the definition excludes them.
This response preserves the exclusion of ẓarf/āla while covering all adjectives.
5
Compare the two responses and their implications
Note that the choice between the two depends on whether one prioritizes avoiding false negatives (missing adjectives) or false positives (including non-adjectives). The passage shows the Hanafi method of rigorous definition through counterexamples and refinement.
In practice, the second response aligns with the majority of grammarians, but the first is also a valid Hanafi view.

ولقائل ان يقول هذا التفسير لا يصدق الا علی صفة يہاں سے صفت کی تعریف پر اعتراض کیا جارہا ہے کہ صفت کی تعریف جامع نہیں ہے کیونکہ صفت کی یہ تعریف کی گئی ہے کہ اس کا معنی بعینہ مشتق منہ والا ہو لیکن وزن مشتق کا ہو یعنی اس کو مشتق کے وزن کے ساتھ تعبیر کیا جائے یہ تعریف فقط اس صفت پر صادق آتی ہے جو مع وزن الفاعل یا مع وزن المفعول ہو باقی صفات جو ان دو وزن پر نہیں باوجود صفت ہونے کے ان پر تعریف صادق نہیں آ رہی کیونکہ ان کو وزن مشتق کے ساتھ تعبیر نہیں کیا جاتا کیونکہ جس کے ساتھ معنی مصدری قائم ہو اس کو بالفاعل یا بالمفعول سے تعبیر کیا جاتا ہے افعل فعلان فعل مستفعل مفعلل وغیرہ سے تعبیر نہیں کیا جاتا حالانکہ یہ تمام صفات ہیں فلیس معنى الابیض یعنی ابیض کا معنی کو یوں تعبیر نہیں کیا جاتا بیاض مع الافعل یا افضل مع الفعل عطشان کا معنی عطش مع الفعلان اور خیر کا معنی خیریت مع الفعل مستخرج کا معنی استخراج مع المستفعل، اور مدحرج کا معنی دحرجہ مع المفعلل نہیں ہے تو یہ تمام صفات ہیں لیکن تعریف ان پر صادق نہیں آ رہی۔ وان منع ذالک یعنی اگر آپ یہ کہیں کہ نہیں تعریف ان تمام پر صادق آرہی ہے اور اس طرح تعبیر کرنا بالکل درست ہے تو پھر ہم کہیں گے کہ اسم ظرف اسم آلہ کا کیا قصور ہے پھر ان کو بھی صفت میں داخل ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ مقتل کا معنی قتل مع المفعل کرنا یہ ابیض کا معنی بیاض مع الافعل اور مدحرج کا معنی دحرجہ مع المفعلل سے زیادہ بعید نہیں ہے تو دونوں مساوی ہیں اگر وہ سارے خارج ہو جاتے ہیں یہ بھی خارج وہ داخل ہیں تو یہ بھی داخل ۔ جواب! اس اعتراض کے دو جواب دینے گئے ہیں (۱) پہلا جواب یہ دیا گیا ہے وزن مشتق سے مراد صرف فاعل و مفعول نہیں بلکہ اس سے مشتق کی ہیئت و شکل مراد ہے تو مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ صفت وہ ہے جس کا معنی بعینه مشتق منہ والا ہو مع ہیئت المشتق یعنی شکل و صورت مشتق والی ہو خواہ وہ ہیئت فاعل والی ہو یا مفعول والی خواہ مفعلل والی مستفعل والی، تو اس میں تمام صفات داخل ہو جائیں گی لیکن سوال یہ ہوگا کہ پھر اسم ظرف مکان زمان آلہ بھی صفت میں داخل ہو جائیں گے حالانکہ جمہور ان کو صفت میں داخل نہیں کرتے تو جواب یہ ہے کہ مصنف کے نزدیک وہ بھی صفت میں داخل ہیں کیونکہ صفت کی تعریف ان پر صادق آرہی ہے باقی رہے جمہور تو مصنف مقام تحقیق میں جمہور کی مخالفت کر لیتے ہیں جیسے پیچھے موضوع کے مباحث میں مخالفت کی ہے (۲) دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ مع وزن المین سے وزن جنس المشتق مراد ہیں یعنی مشتق کا جنس تو جمیع صفات از جنس اسم فاعل والمفعول ہیں بخلاف زمان مکان آلہ کے ان کے اوزان از جنس صفات مشتقہ نہیں ۔
And someone may say: This definition is only true for [some adjectives]. Here an objection is raised against the definition of the adjective (sifat). The definition of the adjective is not comprehensive because it defines the adjective as: its meaning is exactly that of the mushtaqq minhu, but with the weight of the mushtaqq, i.e., it is expressed with the weight of the mushtaqq. This definition only applies to the adjective that is on the weight of fāʿil or mafʿūl. Other adjectives, even though they are adjectives, the definition does not apply to them because they are not expressed with the weight of the mushtaqq. For example, the meaning of abyad is not expressed as bayād with afʿal or afḍal with faʿl, nor ʿaṭshān as ʿaṭash with fuʿlān, nor khayr as khayriyya with faʿl, nor mustakhraj as istikhrāj with mustafʿil, nor mudḥarraj as daḥraj with mufaʿlil. So these are all adjectives, but the definition does not apply to them. If you deny that and say the definition does apply, then we say: what is wrong with ẓarf and āla nouns? They should also be included in adjectives, because the meaning of maqtal as qatl with mafʿal is not more far-fetched than abyad as bayāḍ with afʿal or mudḥarraj as daḥraja with mufaʿlil. So both are equal. If those are excluded, these should also be excluded; if those are included, these should also be included. Answer: Two answers are given to this objection. (1) The first answer: By 'weight of the mushtaqq' is meant not only fāʿil and mafʿūl but rather the form and shape of the mushtaqq. So the definition is: the adjective is that whose meaning is exactly that of the mushtaqq minhu together with the form of the mushtaqq, whether that form is fāʿil, mafʿūl, mufaʿlil, mustafʿil, etc. Thus all adjectives are included. However, the question arises: then ẓarf and āla nouns would also be included in adjectives, while the majority do not include them. The answer is that according to the author they are included because the definition applies to them. As for the majority, the author sometimes opposes them in investigative places, as he earlier opposed them in the discussion on mawḍūʿ. (2) The second answer: By 'weight of the word' is meant the genus of the derivation; i.e., all adjectives are of the genus of ism fāʿil and ism mafʿūl, unlike nouns of time, place, and instrument, whose weights are not of the genus of derived adjectives.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the precise definition of the adjective (ṣifa) in the context of Arabic grammar and its implications for uṣūl al-fiqh. The commentator presents a critique that the standard definition of ṣifa—that it conveys the same meaning as its source (mushtaqq minhu) but with a derived weight—only covers adjectives in the patterns of fāʿil and mafʿūl. Other common adjective patterns like afʿal (e.g., abyad - white), fuʿlān (e.g., ʿaṭshān - thirsty), mustafʿil (e.g., mustakhraj - extracted), and mufaʿlil (e.g., mudḥarraj - rolled) are excluded, even though they are genuine adjectives. If one insists that the definition does apply to these, then nouns of place, time, and instrument (e.g., maqtal - place of killing) would also have to be included, as their derivation is similar. The commentator then provides two responses. The first broadens the definition by interpreting 'weight of the mushtaqq' to mean any derived form, so all adjectives are included. This, however, would also include zarf and āla nouns, but the author accepts this, even against the majority view. The second response narrows the definition by specifying that the 'weight of the mushtaqq' refers specifically to weights that are from the genus of fāʿil and mafʿūl, thereby excluding zarf and āla nouns. This shows the Hanafi method of rigorous definition and debate in linguistic matters that underpin legal interpretation.

Key Terms
صفت (صفة) (ṣifa): A derived word whose meaning is exactly that of its source (mushtaqq minhu) and which is expressed on a derived weight (wazn al-mushtaqq).
وزن مشتق (wazn al-mushtaqq): The morphological pattern of a derived word, such as fāʿil, mafʿūl, afʿal, etc. The debate is whether it includes all patterns or only those of the genus of fāʿil and mafʿūl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second answer in this passage, why are nouns of time, place, and instrument not considered adjectives?
A) Because their meanings are not derived from a source.
B) Because their weights (patterns) are not from the genus of fāʿil and mafʿūl.
C) Because they are always definite.
D) Because the majority of scholars exclude them.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of ṣifa is not monolithic; it is refined through debate to ensure it covers all adjectives while potentially excluding other derived nouns, illustrating the methodical approach of uṣūl al-fiqh to linguistic classification.

Two Types of Ishtiqāq and the Nature of ʿAlam
Explaining two types of derivation and that ʿalam is not derived in its primary sense

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between theoretical and practical derivation (ishtiqāq ʿilmī and ʿamalī) and explain why a proper noun (ʿalam) is not considered derived in its primary sense in Hanafi uṣūl.

Core Idea
Theoretical derivation is mental recognition; practical derivation is linguistic creation—and a proper noun names without describing.

In this passage, the commentator explains two distinct ways words relate to roots. This distinction matters in uṣūl because derived words carry semantic weight for legal reasoning, while proper nouns (like 'Zaid') do not—they are solid (jamid) in their primary function. Understanding this helps you evaluate when a word can be subjected to qiyās or istiḥsān.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of ishtiqāq
Identify the two categories mentioned: theoretical (ʿilmī) and practical (ʿamalī). Note that theoretical is purely cognitive, while practical involves active linguistic creation.
2
Parse the definition of theoretical derivation
Examine the definition: 'that you find a proportion between two words in original meaning and compositional letters'. This is a mental recognition without producing a new word.
3
Parse the definition of practical derivation
Examine the definition: 'that you take from a word what is appropriate to it... and make that word indicative of a meaning'. This involves actively deriving a new word for use.
4
Apply the distinction to the case of ʿalam
Understand that a proper noun (e.g., 'Zaid') in its primary function names an individual without conveying a meaning—it is jamid. Therefore, it is not considered derived, even if it historically originates from a root.
This affects whether it can be used in qiyās.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاشتقاق يفسر تارة باعتبار العلم احتفاق کی قسمیں بیان کر رہے ہیں اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) اشتفاق علمی (۲) عملی اشتقاق علمی، یعنی جو صرف علم کی حد تک ہو اس سے صرف اشتقاق کا علم حاصل ہوگا کوئی تصرف و عمل نہیں ہوگا اس کی تعریف یہ ہے کہ ان تجد بین اللفظين تنا سبا یعنی دو لفظوں میں اصل معنی اور حروف ترکیبیہ میں تناسب پائیں اور علمی درجہ میں ایک کو دوسرے کی طرف رد کریں جس کو رد کر رہے ہیں یہ شقق اور جس کی طرف کیا جا رہا ہے وہ مشتق منہ ہے تو یہ صرف علمی حد تک ہے اس میں عمل کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہے اس لیے اس کو اشتقاق علمی کہتے ہیں۔ اشتقاق عملی، وہ ہے جس میں عمل اور تصرف کو دخل ہے اس کی تعریف یہ کی ہے کہ ان تاخذ من اللفظ ما يناسبه الخ یعنی ایک لفظ سے دوسرا لفظ پکڑیں جو پہلے کے ساتھ حروف اصلیہ اور ترتیب میں مناسبت رکھتا ہو اور اس لفظ کو دال قرار دیں ایسے معنی پر جو لفظ دال کے معنی کے ساتھ مناسبت رکھتا ہو تو لفظ ماخوذ خود کو شتق اور ماخوذ منہ کو مشتق منہ کہا جاتا ہے۔ ولا يخفى ان العلم یہاں سے تفتازانی وضاحت کر رہے ہیں کہ علم کی بحث و قسمیں بیان کی گئی ہیں مشتق جامد تو علم اپنے علمی معنی کے اعتبار سے مشتق نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ اس صورت میں وہ ذات مسمی پر دلالت کرتا ہے اس میں معنی کا لحاظ نہیں ہوتا البتہ اپنے معنی اصلی جنسی کے اعتبار سے مشتق ہو سکتا ہے تو حقیقتا مشتق اسم جنس ہی ہوتا ہے۔
Derivation (ishtiqāq) is explained sometimes by way of knowledge. [The text] is explaining the types of derivation; it has two types: (1) theoretical derivation (ishtiqāq ʿilmī) and (2) practical derivation (ishtiqāq ʿamalī). Theoretical derivation: it is only to the extent of knowledge; from it only knowledge of derivation is obtained, no disposal or action. Its definition is: that you find a proportion between two words in original meaning and compositional letters, and in the theoretical level you refer one to the other. What is being referred is the mushtaqq, and what it is referred to is the mushtaqq minhu. So this is only to the theoretical level; action has no part in it, therefore it is called theoretical derivation. Practical derivation: it is that in which action and disposal have a part. Its definition is: that you take from a word what is appropriate to it, i.e., you take another word that has proportion with the first in original letters and order, and you make that word indicative of a meaning that has proportion with the meaning of the first word. Then the taken word is called mushtaqq and the source is called mushtaqq minhu. It is not hidden that the proper noun (ʿalam) [is discussed]. Here Taftāzānī is clarifying that the discussion and types of ʿalam have been mentioned—derived or non-derived. So ʿalam in its primary meaning cannot be derived, because in that case it indicates the named entity itself; there is no consideration of meaning. However, with respect to its original generic meaning it can be derived, so in reality the derived one is the common noun (ism al-jins).
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage defines two types of linguistic derivation (ishtiqāq) relevant to uṣūl al-fiqh: theoretical (ʿilmī) and practical (ʿamalī). Theoretical derivation is simply recognizing a relation between two words without generating new words; practical derivation involves actively creating a new word that is morphologically and semantically related. The commentator then addresses the proper noun (ʿalam), such as 'Zaid'. In its primary function, a proper noun is not considered derived because it directly names an individual without conveying a meaning; it is 'jamid' (solid). However, from a secondary perspective, some proper nouns may have originated from descriptive words (e.g., 'Ḥātim' from 'ḥatm' - to decide), in which case they are considered derived in terms of origin. This distinction is important in uṣūl because derived words often carry legal implications based on their meanings, while proper nouns do not.

Key Terms
اشتقاق (ishtiqāq): Linguistic derivation; the relation between a derived word and its root. Two types: theoretical (ʿilmī) and practical (ʿamalī).
علم (ʿalam): A proper noun that designates a specific entity without conveying a descriptive meaning. In its primary sense, it is jamid (non-derived).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the key difference between theoretical and practical derivation?
A) Theoretical derivation involves action; practical derivation does not.
B) Theoretical derivation is only recognizing a relation; practical derivation involves creating new words.
C) Theoretical derivation applies only to nouns; practical derivation applies to verbs.
D) There is no difference; both are the same.

Key Takeaway
The two types of derivation—theoretical and practical—differ in the presence of action; proper nouns are not derived in their primary function, which affects their use in legal reasoning.
